BabySteps AI School — Functional Specification Document
Document ID: BS-FSD-2026-001 | Version: 1.0 | Date: February 7, 2026 | Classification: Confidential
Reference PRD: BS-PRD-2026-002 v2.0
1. INTRODUCTION
1.1 Purpose
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
This document translates the BabySteps PRD v2.0 into implementable, testable functional and non-functional requirements. Phase 1 is specified at full engineering detail. Phases 2–4 are described at feature level and will be elaborated in subsequent FSD releases prior to each phase start.
1.2 Requirement ID Convention
BS-[MODULE]-[SEQ]-[F/NF] where MODULE is a 3-letter code, SEQ is a 3-digit number, F = Functional, NF = Non-Functional.
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
1.3 Priority Definitions
1.4 Phase 1 Delivery Summary
Phase 1: Foundation (Months 1–3, Mar–May 2026)
Delivery: Private Alpha — 500 families, CBSE Grades 1–5, Hindi + English, Android app.
What a student can do at end of Phase 1:
Parent registers with mobile + OTP, completes DPDP consent, creates child profile
Child logs in with picture-code (ages 3–6) or PIN (ages 6–12)
Child takes a 10–15 minute diagnostic → system assigns IQ Level (1/2/3)
Child selects their three languages during onboarding
AI Teacher delivers CBSE Math and English/Hindi concepts for Grades 1–5, adapted to IQ Level
Child answers practice questions and earns 1–5 star ratings
Child cannot progress until achieving 3 stars (mastery gate enforced)
If child doesn't understand, AI reteaches using a different strategy
Child sees a star map dashboard with streaks
Parent sees child's progress, stars, time spent, and daily summary
Parent pays via UPI/Razorpay for Standard subscription
Everything runs on a ₹8,000 Android phone over 4G

3. PHASE 1 DETAILED FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENTS
3.1 MODULE: AUTHENTICATION (AUT)
BS-AUT-001-F | Parent Registration via Mobile + OTP
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Parents register using their Indian mobile number. System sends a 6-digit OTP via SMS. Verified parents create their profile.
Preconditions: None (first-time user).
Input Flow:
Parent taps "Register" on the app home screen
Screen 1 — Phone Number Entry:
◦ Country code dropdown (default: +91 India), pre-selected
◦ 10-digit mobile number input field (numeric keyboard auto-shown)
◦ "Send OTP" button (disabled until 10 digits entered)
Validation: If number is not 10 digits (India) or not valid E.164 format (international), show inline error: "Please enter a valid mobile number"
System calls SMS gateway API (MSG91 or Twilio) to send 6-digit OTP
Screen 2 — OTP Verification:
◦ 6 individual digit input boxes (auto-advance on entry)
◦ Countdown timer: "Resend OTP in 0:30"
◦ After 30 seconds: "Resend OTP" link becomes active
◦ "Verify" button
If OTP matches: Proceed to Screen 3
If OTP wrong: Shake animation on input boxes + "Incorrect OTP. Try again." + allow 3 retries
After 3 failures: "Too many attempts. Try again in 15 minutes." — lock the number for 15 min
If OTP expired (5 min): "OTP expired. Tap Resend."
Screen 3 — Profile Completion:
◦ Full Name (mandatory, 2–100 characters, Unicode supported for Indian names)
◦ Email (optional, validated format)
◦ State / Union Territory (mandatory, dropdown with all 36 options + "Outside India")
◦ If "Outside India" selected: Country dropdown appears
◦ Preferred Language for the app interface (mandatory, default based on state: e.g., Maharashtra→Marathi, Tamil Nadu→Tamil, else Hindi)
◦ "Create Account" button
On submit: Create parent record, issue JWT token, redirect to Add Child flow
API Specification:
POST /api/v1/auth/send-otp
Request: { "mobile": "+919876543210" }
Response 200: { "otp_id": "uuid", "expires_in": 300 }
Response 429: { "error": "rate_limited", "retry_after": 900 }
POST /api/v1/auth/verify-otp
Request: { "otp_id": "uuid", "otp_code": "123456" }
Response 200: { "temp_token": "jwt...", "next_step": "complete_profile" }
Response 401: { "error": "invalid_otp", "attempts_remaining": 2 }
POST /api/v1/auth/complete-registration
Headers: Authorization: Bearer <temp_token>
Request: { "full_name": "Priya Sharma", "email": "priya@email.com", "state": "maharashtra", "preferred_language": "mr" }
Response 201: { "parent_id": "uuid", "access_token": "jwt...", "refresh_token": "jwt..." }
Database Table: parents
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: OTP delivered within 10 seconds for Indian numbers, 30 seconds international
• AC2: Full registration flow (phone → OTP → profile) completes in under 2 minutes on 4G
• AC3: Duplicate number shows "Already registered. Tap to login."
• AC4: Name field accepts Devanagari, Tamil, Telugu, Bengali, and all Indian scripts
• AC5: Dropdown shows states in the user's preferred language
• AC6: Rate limit: Max 5 OTP requests per phone number per hour
BS-AUT-002-F | DPDP Act — Verifiable Parental Consent
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Before ANY child data is collected, the parent MUST read and explicitly consent to data processing per the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023. Consent must be verifiable — the system records what was shown, when, and how consent was confirmed.
Trigger: When parent taps "Add Child" for the first time (before the child profile form appears).
Input Flow:
System displays a full-screen Consent Notice in the parent's preferred language
Consent Notice contents (mandatory per DPDP Act Section 6):
◦ What data we collect: Child's first name, date of birth, voice recordings during lessons, learning progress data, question responses, time-on-platform data
◦ Why we collect it: To deliver personalised AI-driven education to your child
◦ How it is used: Data is processed by AI models to adapt teaching to your child's learning level. Data is never used for advertising. Data is never sold to third parties.
◦ Who has access: You (the parent), your child's assigned mentor (if applicable), and BabySteps system administrators for technical support
◦ How long we keep it: Learning data is kept for the duration of enrollment + 1 year. Voice recordings are processed and auto-deleted within 30 days unless you choose to retain them.
◦ Your rights: You can withdraw consent at any time. You can request a copy of all data. You can request deletion of all data. Contact our Data Protection Officer at dpo@babysteps.in
Parent must scroll to the bottom of the notice (scroll tracking confirms full read)
Checkbox: "I, [auto-filled parent name], give consent for BabySteps to process my child's personal data as described above"
Checkbox is unchecked by default — parent must actively check it
"I Agree" button (disabled until checkbox is checked AND full scroll confirmed)
Identity Verification — one of:
◦ Method A (preferred): Aadhaar + OTP via DigiLocker — System redirects to DigiLocker OAuth. Parent authenticates. DigiLocker returns verified name + masked Aadhaar. System records DigiLocker verification ID.
◦ Method B: Virtual ID — Parent enters Aadhaar Virtual ID + OTP sent to Aadhaar-linked mobile
◦ Method C: Credit/debit card micro-charge — ₹1 charge to parent's card (refunded) confirms identity via card holder name match. For parents without Aadhaar.
On successful verification: Consent record created (immutable), child profile form is displayed
API Specification:
GET /api/v1/consent/notice?language=hi
Response 200: { "notice_id": "uuid", "version": "1.0", "text": "...", "language": "hi" }
POST /api/v1/consent/grant
Headers: Authorization: Bearer <parent_token>
Request: {
"notice_id": "uuid",
"notice_version": "1.0",
"scroll_completed": true,
"checkbox_checked": true,
"verification_method": "digilocker",
"verification_reference": "DL-xxxx-yyyy",
"device_info": { "os": "Android 12", "device": "Samsung M31", "app_version": "1.0.0" },
"ip_address": "auto-captured"
}
Response 201: { "consent_id": "uuid", "status": "granted", "child_creation_unlocked": true }
POST /api/v1/consent/withdraw
Headers: Authorization: Bearer <parent_token>
Request: { "consent_id": "uuid", "reason": "optional text" }
Response 200: { "status": "withdrawn", "data_deletion_initiated": true, "deletion_deadline": "2026-06-10T00:00:00Z" }
Database Table: consent_records (APPEND-ONLY — no UPDATE or DELETE)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Child profile form is BLOCKED until consent is granted — enforced server-side (API rejects child creation without valid consent_id)
• AC2: Consent notice is displayed in parent's preferred language (Hindi and English minimum Phase 1)
• AC3: "I Agree" button stays disabled until both checkbox AND full-scroll are confirmed
• AC4: Consent record is immutable — database permissions prevent UPDATE/DELETE on this table
• AC5: Consent withdrawal triggers data deletion workflow: all child data marked for deletion within 72 hours
• AC6: DigiLocker flow completes within 60 seconds
• AC7: Full Aadhaar number is NEVER stored — only DigiLocker verification reference
BS-AUT-003-F | Student Profile Creation
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: After consent is granted, the parent creates the child's profile with minimum necessary data.
Input Flow:
Screen: "Tell us about your child"
Fields:
◦ First Name (mandatory, 1–50 chars, Unicode)
◦ Display Name / Nickname (optional — shown in the UI to the child; if blank, First Name is used)
◦ Date of Birth (mandatory, date picker, range: today minus 18 years to today minus 3 years)
◦ Gender (optional: Boy / Girl / Prefer not to say — 3 large tappable cards with icons)
◦ Current Class/Grade (mandatory, scrollable list: Nursery, LKG, UKG, Class 1 through Class 12, "Not in school")
◦ Curriculum Board (mandatory: CBSE / ICSE / State Board [with state sub-selection] / Other / Not applicable. Phase 1: only CBSE active; others show "Coming soon in [month]")
◦ Primary Language at Home (mandatory, dropdown: top 15 Indian languages + English, sorted by state-relevance)
On submit: System calculates age group from DOB:
◦ 3–6 years → age_group = '3-6', login_method = 'picture'
◦ 6–12 years → age_group = '6-12', login_method = 'pin'
◦ 12–18 years → age_group = '12-18', login_method = 'password'
Redirect to Avatar Selection screen: 12 avatar options (6 boy-presenting, 6 girl-presenting, all culturally Indian — e.g., child in kurta, child with bindi, child playing cricket, child reading under a banyan tree)
Redirect to Login Setup screen based on age group (see BS-AUT-004-F, BS-AUT-005-F)
Student record created
API Specification:
POST /api/v1/students
Headers: Authorization: Bearer <parent_token>
Request: {
"consent_id": "uuid",
"first_name": "Aarav",
"display_name": "Aaru",
"date_of_birth": "2019-06-15",
"gender": "male",
"current_grade": "class_1",
"curriculum_board": "cbse",
"primary_home_language": "hi",
"avatar_id": "avatar_cricket_boy"
}
Response 201: {
"student_id": "uuid",
"age_group": "6-12",
"login_method": "pin",
"next_step": "setup_login"
}
Response 403: { "error": "consent_not_granted" }
Database Table: students
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Profile creation is rejected if consent_id is invalid or consent is withdrawn
• AC2: DOB validates: child must be 3–18 years old at time of creation
• AC3: Parent can add up to 5 children under one account
• AC4: Avatar selection works with single tap on large tiles (80x80dp minimum)
• AC5: Created student immediately appears in parent dashboard
• AC6: Phase 1: Only CBSE board is selectable; others show "Coming soon"
BS-AUT-004-F | Student Login — Picture-Based (Ages 3–6)
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Children aged 3–6 log in by tapping their avatar, then selecting 3 pictures in sequence from a grid.
Setup Flow (during profile creation):
System displays instruction to parent: "Help your child choose 3 secret pictures"
A 4×3 grid of 12 pictures is displayed (large tiles 80×80dp): Lotus, Mango, Peacock, Elephant, Cricket Bat, Sun, Moon, Star, Fish, Butterfly, Cow, Train
Parent and child together tap 3 pictures in their chosen order
System confirms: "Your secret pictures are: [Pic1] → [Pic2] → [Pic3]. Remember this!"
Sequence is hashed (bcrypt) and stored
Login Flow:
App home screen shows all student avatars registered on this device (large cards with display name + avatar image, voice narration of name)
Child taps their avatar → voice says "Hello [Display Name]! Tap your secret pictures!"
Same 4×3 grid appears. Pictures are in RANDOMISED positions (different from setup)
Child taps 3 pictures in the correct sequence
Each tap: Picture bounces + sparkle animation + pleasant sound
If correct: Confetti animation + "Welcome back, [Name]!" + redirect to dashboard
If wrong: Friendly wobble animation + "Oops, let's try again!" + grid re-randomises
After 5 wrong attempts: "Let's get a grown-up to help!" + Parent unlock screen (parent enters OTP or device PIN)
Successful login creates a session (JWT, 24-hour expiry)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Grid randomises picture positions on every login attempt (prevents positional memory)
• AC2: All interactions work without any text reading by the child
• AC3: Audio feedback accompanies every action
• AC4: Login completes in under 15 seconds for a child who knows their pictures
• AC5: Works on 4-inch screens (grid adapts to screen size)
• AC6: Parent can reset secret pictures from parent app
• AC7: After 5 failures, device locks for 5 minutes for that student (parent override available)
BS-AUT-005-F | Student Login — PIN-Based (Ages 6–12)
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Students aged 6–12 log in by tapping their avatar, then entering a 4-digit PIN on a numeric keypad.
Setup Flow: Parent sets the 4-digit PIN during profile creation. Student is shown the PIN and asked to enter it once to confirm.
Login Flow:
Student taps their avatar on home screen
"Hi [Name]! Enter your PIN" with a large 3×4+1 numeric keypad (1–9, 0, backspace, enter)
Each digit entered shows a filled dot (●) — PIN is masked
On 4th digit: auto-submit (no need to tap Enter)
If correct: Welcome animation + dashboard
If wrong: Shake + "Try again!" + allow 5 attempts
After 5 failures: Parent unlock required
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Keypad buttons are minimum 56×56dp with 8dp spacing
• AC2: PIN is never displayed on screen (always masked)
• AC3: PIN hash is bcrypt (cost 12), never stored in plain text
• AC4: Parent can reset PIN from parent dashboard (triggers OTP to parent's phone)
• AC5: Auto-submit on 4th digit reduces friction
BS-AUT-006-F | Parent Login — Mobile + OTP
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Parents log in to the parent dashboard via mobile + OTP or remembered device.
Flow: Same as registration OTP flow, but on existing account:
Parent enters registered mobile number
System verifies number exists → sends OTP
Correct OTP → JWT issued → parent dashboard
"Remember this device for 30 days" option — stores encrypted device fingerprint; subsequent visits auto-login
API Specification:
POST /api/v1/auth/login/send-otp
Request: { "mobile": "+919876543210" }
Response 200: { "otp_id": "uuid" }
Response 404: { "error": "not_registered", "suggestion": "register" }
POST /api/v1/auth/login/verify-otp
Request: { "otp_id": "uuid", "otp_code": "123456", "remember_device": true }
Response 200: {
"access_token": "jwt...",
"refresh_token": "jwt...",
"parent_id": "uuid",
"children": [{ "student_id": "uuid", "display_name": "Aaru", "avatar_id": "..." }]
}
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Remembered device login requires zero taps (auto-detects and logs in)
• AC2: Parent can view/revoke remembered devices from settings
• AC3: JWT access token expires in 1 hour; refresh token in 30 days
• AC4: Concurrent sessions allowed on up to 3 devices
BS-AUT-007-F | Three-Language Selection During Onboarding
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: After student profile creation, parent and student choose 3 languages per the NEP 2020 Three-Language Formula.
Flow:
Screen: "Choose [Child Name]'s Three Languages" with explanation: "As per India's education policy, every child learns 3 languages."
Language 1 — Mother Tongue / Regional Language:
◦ Auto-suggested based on parent's state (e.g., Maharashtra → Marathi)
◦ Dropdown with all 22 Scheduled Languages + English
◦ Label: "Your home language"
Language 2:
◦ Smart suggestion: If L1 is Hindi → suggest English. If L1 is non-Hindi → suggest Hindi or English
◦ Same dropdown
◦ Validation: Cannot be same as L1
Language 3:
◦ Smart suggestion: If L1 is regional and L2 is Hindi → suggest English. If L1 is regional and L2 is English → suggest Hindi.
◦ Same dropdown
◦ Validation: Cannot be same as L1 or L2
Validation bar at bottom: Displays "✓ At least 2 Indian languages selected" or "✗ At least 2 languages must be native to India" (per NEP 2020 rule)
System note: "Your child will also learn basic Sanskrit as part of the cultural curriculum."
Confirm: "These are [Child Name]'s languages: [L1], [L2], [L3]" with Edit option
On confirm: Stored in student record. Medium of instruction for ages 3–8 defaults to L1.
Phase 1 Languages Available: Hindi (hi), English (en) — only these two are fully active for content delivery. Other languages can be selected but will show "Content in [language] coming soon — we'll teach in Hindi/English for now."
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Auto-suggestion is correct for all 36 Indian states/UTs
• AC2: System blocks selection of fewer than 2 Indian languages
• AC3: Duplicate language selection is prevented inline
• AC4: Selections are stored and can be changed later from parent settings
• AC5: Phase 1 gracefully handles language selections where content isn't yet available
BS-AUT-008-F | Role-Based Access Control Engine
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Every API request is authorised against the user's role and data scope. Enforced at both API middleware and database (row-level security) layers.
Phase 1 Roles:
Enforcement Logic (every API request):
Extract JWT from Authorization: Bearer <token> header
Validate JWT: Check signature (RS256), expiry, issuer
Extract claims: sub (user_id), role, iat, exp
API middleware checks: Is this role allowed to call this endpoint? (whitelist per role)
If endpoint is allowed, inject scope predicate into database query:
◦ Student calling GET /progress → SELECT * FROM concept_mastery WHERE student_id = $jwt.sub
◦ Parent calling GET /children/:id/progress → SELECT * FROM concept_mastery WHERE student_id = $child_id AND EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM students WHERE student_id = $child_id AND parent_id = $jwt.sub)
If role check fails: Return HTTP 403 + log to audit_log
If scope check fails (e.g., parent trying to access unlinked child): Return HTTP 403 + log to audit_log
Database Table: audit_log (APPEND-ONLY, partitioned by month)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Student A's JWT CANNOT retrieve Student B's data — verified via automated penetration test
• AC2: Parent can ONLY access their own linked children — cross-parent access blocked
• AC3: Every denied request is logged with full context
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
• AC4: JWT with expired token returns 401 (not 403)
• AC5: Audit log table cannot be modified via application code (enforced by DB permissions)
3.2 MODULE: ONBOARDING DIAGNOSTIC (DIA)
BS-DIA-001-F | IQ Level Diagnostic — Ages 3–6
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: An interactive, game-like diagnostic assessment determines the child's initial IQ Level. Entirely voice-and-touch-based with no reading required.
Structure: 15 tasks across 4 domains
Domain 1: Pattern Recognition (5 tasks)
Domain 2: Vocabulary (4 tasks) — AI voice speaks in Language 1 (Hindi/English)
Domain 3: Numeracy (4 tasks)
Domain 4: Instruction Following (2 tasks)
Adaptive Logic:
• Tasks presented in order above (easy → hard within each domain)
• If child gets tasks 1–2 wrong in a domain, skip remaining hard tasks in that domain (move to next domain)
• Total time: 8–12 minutes with generous 30-second timeout per task
IQ Level Calculation:
UI Requirements:
• Every task has AI voice narration in Language 1
• Answer options are large tappable tiles (minimum 80×80dp)
• Correct answer: Star burst animation + "Yay!" sound (regardless of answer — no negative feedback)
• Wrong answer: Same positive animation (child doesn't know they got it wrong)
• Progress: 15 dots at bottom of screen, filling as tasks complete
• "Take a break" option (parent can pause and resume within 24 hours)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Assessment completes in 8–12 minutes
• AC2: ZERO text appears on any task screen — everything is visual + audio
• AC3: All audio is in child's Language 1 (Hindi or English for Phase 1)
• AC4: Result is shown to parent as "Your child's Learning Level: [Foundation/Standard/Advanced]" — the word "IQ" is NEVER shown to parents or children
• AC5: Result is stored in student record and learning path adapts immediately
• AC6: If child abandons mid-assessment, progress is saved and they can resume within 24 hours
BS-DIA-002-F | IQ Level Diagnostic — Ages 6–12
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Adaptive diagnostic using Item Response Theory (IRT) to assess Math, Reading, and Logical Reasoning abilities and assign IQ Level.
Structure: 25 items, adaptive difficulty
Item Pool (minimum for Phase 1):
• Math: 50 calibrated items across Easy/Medium/Hard (addition, subtraction, multiplication, fractions, word problems for Grades 1–5)
• Reading Comprehension: 30 calibrated items (passage-based questions in Hindi and English)
• Logical Reasoning: 20 calibrated items (sequences, odd-one-out, analogies)
IRT 3PL Adaptive Algorithm:
Start with a medium-difficulty item (b = 0.0)
After student responds, update ability estimate (θ) using Bayesian updating
Select next item that maximises Fisher information at current θ estimate
Repeat until: Standard Error of θ < 0.30 OR 25 items administered
Final θ estimate determines IQ Level:
◦ θ < -0.5 → Level 1 (Foundation)
◦ -0.5 ≤ θ ≤ +0.5 → Level 2 (Standard)
◦ θ > +0.5 → Level 3 (Advanced)
Item Types: MCQ (4 options), numeric fill-in-blank (calculator disabled), True/False
Time Limits: 60 seconds per Math item, 90 seconds per Reading item, 45 seconds per Reasoning item. Total: 15–20 minutes.
UI Requirements:
• Clean, distraction-free assessment interface
• Question number and progress bar at top
• Timer visible but not anxiety-inducing (no colour change until 10 seconds left)
• "Skip" button available (skipped items scored as incorrect for IRT estimation)
• AI voice reads each question aloud (toggle-able by student)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: IRT engine converges (SE < 0.3) within 20 items for 80% of students
• AC2: Item selection is demonstrably adaptive (observed difficulty tracks student ability)
• AC3: Assessment completes in 15–20 minutes
• AC4: Results show per-subject placement: "Math: Grade 3 level, Reading: Grade 2 level, Reasoning: Grade 4 level"
• AC5: Full item-response data stored for future psychometric analysis
• AC6: Parent sees summary: "Learning Level: [X]" + "Recommended starting point: [grade/subject details]"
3.3 MODULE: AI TEACHING ENGINE (AIE)
BS-AIE-001-F | AI Teacher — Concept Lesson Delivery
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: For every concept in the learning path, the AI Teacher generates a personalised lesson adapted to the student's IQ Level, delivering it via text + TTS narration.
Flow:
Student's dashboard shows the next unlocked concept. Student taps to start.
System retrieves: concept metadata (from concepts table), curriculum content chunks (from RAG vector DB), student's IQ Level, student's age group, student's Language 1, student's performance on prerequisite concepts
System constructs an LLM prompt:
System: You are a warm, patient AI teacher for Indian children.
The student is [age] years old, in [grade], studying [subject] at [IQ Level] level.
Their language is [Language 1]. They have mastered the following prerequisites: [list].
Teaching style for [IQ Level]:
- Level 1: Use very simple words. Give 5-7 examples from Indian daily life (buying vegetables at sabzi mandi, sharing rotis, counting cricket runs). Go step by step. Use analogies. Be very encouraging.
- Level 2: Use clear explanations with 3-4 examples. Balance simplicity with mild challenge.
- Level 3: Be concise. Provide 1-2 examples then challenge with deeper questions. Connect to other subjects.
Curriculum context (from RAG):
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
[Retrieved curriculum chunks for this concept]
Generate a lesson for the concept: [Concept Name]
Include: Introduction (why this matters), Explanation, Examples, Summary.
Do NOT include practice questions — those come separately.
Output in [Language 1].
LLM (LLaMA 3.3 70B via vLLM) generates lesson content
Content passes through safety pipeline (BS-AIE-004-F)
Content is rendered in the student UI:
◦ Ages 3–6: AI character narrates (TTS), screen shows illustrations + keywords. Text is minimal. Student listens and watches.
◦ Ages 6–12: Text displayed in scrollable cards with illustrations. AI narrates simultaneously (synchronised word highlighting). Student can pause, replay, adjust speed.
Model Configuration:
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Lesson generates in under 5 seconds end-to-end (prompt → LLM → safety check → TTS → render)
• AC2: Level 1 lessons use measurably simpler vocabulary than Level 3 (Flesch-Kincaid readability difference ≥ 2 grade levels)
• AC3: All examples are India-contextual (Indian names, ₹ currency, Indian foods, Indian sports/festivals)
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
• AC4: Math lessons from DeepSeek-R1 show clear step-by-step working
• AC5: Lesson content aligns with CBSE curriculum for the specified concept (verified by RAG sources cited)
• AC6: Content passes safety pipeline with zero unsafe content
BS-AIE-002-F | AI Teacher — Interactive Tutoring Conversation
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: During any lesson, the student can ask questions via voice or text. The AI responds conversationally using Socratic method for conceptual questions.
Flow:
Persistent microphone/keyboard icon visible during all lesson and practice screens
Student taps mic → recording indicator shown → student speaks → release to send
Voice → Whisper STT → text transcript displayed
Alternatively, students ages 6+ can type in a text input field
AI processes the question:
◦ If conceptual (e.g., "Why does this work?"): Socratic response — ask a guiding question back
◦ If factual (e.g., "What is 7x8?"): Provide the answer with brief explanation
◦ If off-topic (e.g., "Tell me a joke"): Gentle redirect: "Ha! Let's finish learning about [concept] first, then we can take a fun break!"
◦ If unsafe (detected by Llama Guard): Block + redirect: "Let's focus on our lesson!"
Conversation context: Last 10 turns are included in the LLM prompt for continuity
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
Every exchange logged: timestamp, student input (text), AI response (text), classification (conceptual/factual/off-topic/unsafe)
API Specification:
POST /api/v1/tutor/chat
Headers: Authorization: Bearer <student_token>
Request: {
"student_id": "uuid",
"session_id": "uuid",
"concept_id": "uuid",
"message": "Why do we need to carry over in addition?",
"input_type": "voice_transcription"
}
Response 200: {
"response": "Great question! Think about this — if you have 8 sweets and get 5 more, that's 13. But the ones column can only hold up to 9. Where does the extra 1 go? What do you think?",
"response_type": "socratic",
"turn_number": 3
}
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Response latency < 2 seconds from input to rendered response
• AC2: Voice transcription accuracy > 85% for Indian-accented child speech
• AC3: Socratic method used for > 80% of conceptual questions (measured by response_type logging)
• AC4: Off-topic conversations redirected within 2 exchanges
• AC5: Unsafe inputs blocked with 100% effectiveness (zero tolerance)
• AC6: Full conversation log accessible to parent via parent dashboard
BS-AIE-003-F | AI Teacher — Reteaching with Different Strategy
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: When a student achieves < 3 stars, the AI reteaches using a fundamentally different approach, not repeating the same lesson.
Strategy Pool:
Algorithm:
After star rating < 3, system checks which strategies have been tried for this student-concept pair
Select next untried strategy. Priority order varies by student profile:
◦ Level 1, ages 3–6: S1 → S5 → S2 → S4 → S6
◦ Level 1, ages 6–12: S3 → S2 → S4 → S1 → S5 → S6
◦ Level 2: S3 → S2 → S1 → S7 → S6
◦ Level 3: S7 → S2 → S3 → S6
Generate new lesson with selected strategy's prompt template
Student completes reteaching → new practice questions (different from first set) → re-score
If still < 3 stars: Try next strategy. If all strategies exhausted (max 5 attempts): Flag for mentor intervention.
Data Captured:
Table: reteaching_log
- log_id: UUID PK
- student_id: UUID FK
- concept_id: UUID FK
- attempt_number: INTEGER (1-5)
- strategy_used: VARCHAR(10) -- S1, S2, etc.
- star_rating_before: INTEGER
- star_rating_after: INTEGER
- time_spent_minutes: DECIMAL
- completed_at: TIMESTAMP
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Reteaching uses a different strategy each time (verified by strategy_used log)
• AC2: After 5 failed reteaching attempts, mentor alert is sent within 15 minutes
• AC3: 80% of students reach 3 stars within 3 reteaching attempts (tracked metric)
• AC4: Strategy selection adapts to student's profile (Level 1 gets more scaffolded strategies first)
BS-AIE-004-F | Content Safety Pipeline
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: All AI-generated content passes through a multi-stage safety pipeline before reaching the student.
Pipeline (executed sequentially):
If any stage fails:
• Stage 3 fail (unsafe): Regenerate with stronger safety prompt (max 2 retries, then serve pre-approved fallback content)
• Stage 4 fail (off-topic): Regenerate with topic-enforcement prompt
• Stage 5 fail (PII): Strip detected PII and serve cleaned output
• Stage 6 fail (vocabulary): Auto-simplify complex words using a simplification model
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Total pipeline adds < 500ms beyond base LLM generation time
• AC2: 100% of content passes through all stages — no bypass exists
• AC3: False positive rate (safe content blocked) < 3%
• AC4: All pipeline decisions are logged (stage, result, latency)
• AC5: Fallback content is available for every Phase 1 concept (pre-written human content used when AI generation repeatedly fails)
BS-AIE-005-F | Text-to-Speech Engine
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: AI-generated lesson text is narrated via natural-sounding TTS in Hindi and English (Phase 1).
Technical Specification:
Features:
• Word-level timestamps for synchronised text highlighting
• Speed control: 0.75x (slow), 1.0x (default), 1.25x (fast)
• Auto-speed: System defaults ages 3–6 to 0.85x, ages 6–12 to 1.0x
• Caching: Generated audio for identical text cached in Redis (24-hour TTL)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Time to first audio < 500ms from render
• AC2: Word highlighting synchronisation within ±200ms
• AC3: Audio sounds natural and warm (not robotic) — validated by user testing
• AC4: Hindi pronunciation validated by native speakers
• AC5: Works on device speakers without external audio
BS-AIE-006-F | Speech-to-Text for Student Voice Input
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Student voice is captured and transcribed for tutoring conversation input. Fine-tuned for Indian child voices.
Technical Specification:
Flow:
Student taps and holds mic button (or taps once to toggle recording on/off)
Visual recording indicator: Pulsing red circle + waveform animation
Audio sent to Whisper via API (or processed on-device if offline)
Transcription returned and displayed to student
Student can accept or re-record
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Recording starts within 200ms of tap
• AC2: Transcription returned within 2 seconds for 30-second clips
• AC3: WER < 15% for Hindi and English child speech (validated on test dataset of 500 clips)
• AC4: Background noise handling: Acceptable in typical Indian home (TV, family conversations, fans)
• AC5: Microphone permission requested with child-friendly explanation
3.4 MODULE: 5-STAR MASTERY SYSTEM (STR)
BS-STR-001-F | Practice Question Delivery
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: After each lesson, the system presents practice questions from the concept's question bank, adapting difficulty based on performance.
Question Count by IQ Level:
• Level 1: 12–15 questions (starting Easy, moving to Medium)
• Level 2: 8–10 questions (starting Medium)
• Level 3: 5–7 questions (starting Medium, moving to Hard)
Question Types (Phase 1):
• Multiple Choice (MCQ): 4 options, single correct, tap to select
• Numeric Fill-in-Blank: Student types a number, exact match or ±tolerance
• True/False: 2-option MCQ variant
• Drag-and-Drop Ordering: Arrange 3–5 items in sequence
Adaptive Flow:
• After 2 consecutive correct: Increase difficulty by one level
• After 2 consecutive incorrect: Decrease difficulty by one level
• Mix of difficulty levels: Never more than 3 consecutive questions at same difficulty
Immediate Feedback Per Question:
• Correct: Green checkmark animation + "Well done!" + 1-sentence explanation of why correct
• Incorrect: Orange animation + "Not quite — here's a hint:" + explanation showing the correct approach (NOT just the correct answer)
• Audio feedback accompanies visual for ages 3–8
Data Captured Per Response:
Table: question_responses
- response_id: UUID PK
- student_id: UUID FK NOT NULL
- concept_id: UUID FK NOT NULL
- question_id: UUID FK NOT NULL
- session_id: UUID FK NOT NULL
- difficulty: ENUM('easy','medium','hard','expert')
- student_answer: TEXT
- is_correct: BOOLEAN
- partial_credit: DECIMAL(3,2)
- time_taken_seconds: INTEGER
- hints_used: INTEGER DEFAULT 0
- attempt_number: INTEGER DEFAULT 1
- answered_at: TIMESTAMP NOT NULL
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Next question loads within 1 second
• AC2: Feedback appears within 500ms of answer submission
• AC3: Drag-and-drop works smoothly on touch with minimum 48dp drag targets
• AC4: Every response is persisted to the database (no data loss even on app crash — local queue syncs)
• AC5: Adaptive difficulty correctly adjusts after 2 consecutive same-direction results
BS-STR-002-F | Star Rating Calculation (Phase 1 — Basic)
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Calculate 1–5 star rating based on practice question performance. Phase 1 uses a simple percentage-based calculation (self-explanation weighting added in Phase 2).
Calculation:
percentage_correct = (correct_answers / total_questions) × 100
Stars:
0–20% → 1 star
21–40% → 2 stars
41–60% → 3 stars (MINIMUM PASS)
61–80% → 4 stars
81–100% → 5 stars
Display:
• Animated star-filling sequence (each star fills from left to right, gold colour)
• Stars 1–2: Encouraging message: "You're learning! Let's try a different way to understand this."
• Star 3: Celebration: "You did it! ⭐⭐⭐ You understand [concept]!"
• Stars 4–5: Big celebration: "Amazing! You really know this! ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐"
• Star count added to student's total_stars counter
Database Table: concept_mastery
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Star rating calculated and displayed within 2 seconds
• AC2: Star animation plays fully (1.5 seconds for full sequence)
• AC3: If < 3 stars: System immediately transitions to reteaching (BS-AIE-003-F)
• AC4: If ≥ 3 stars: Next concept is unlocked in the learning path
• AC5: Star count in student dashboard updates in real-time
BS-STR-003-F | Mastery Gate — Progression Lock
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Students CANNOT access the next concept in the learning path until achieving ≥ 3 stars on the current concept. Enforced both client-side (UI lock) and server-side (API rejection).
Behaviour:
• Locked concepts show a lock icon and greyed-out appearance
• Tapping a locked concept: Friendly tooltip "Earn 3 stars in [Current Concept] to unlock this!"
• Unlocking animation: Lock breaks open + star burst when 3 stars achieved
• Student CAN navigate back to already-mastered concepts (for review)
• Student CAN switch to a different subject (not locked across subjects)
Server Enforcement:
GET /api/v1/lessons/:concept_id
→ Check: Do all prerequisite concepts have star_rating >= 3 in concept_mastery?
→ If yes: Return lesson content
→ If no: Return 403 { "error": "prerequisites_not_met", "missing": ["concept_uuid_1"] }
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Locked state is enforced at API level — cannot be bypassed by modifying the client
• AC2: Lock/unlock state syncs within 2 seconds of star rating change
• AC3: Subject-switching is unrestricted (student stuck in Math can do English)
• AC4: Unlock animation is satisfying and motivating (user-tested with children)
3.5 MODULE: CURRICULUM AND CONTENT (CUR)
BS-CUR-001-F | Knowledge Graph — Concept DAG
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Curriculum concepts are organised as a directed acyclic graph (DAG) with prerequisite edges. The student's learning path is a topological traversal of this graph.
Phase 1 Scope: ~200 concepts covering CBSE Math (Grades 1–5) and English/Hindi Language (Grades 1–5).
Example Graph Fragment (Math Grade 3):
Counting 1-100 → Addition (single digit) → Addition (double digit) → Addition (triple digit)
→ Subtraction (single digit) → Subtraction (double digit)
Counting 1-100 → Skip Counting by 2s → Multiplication concept → Times tables (2,3,4,5)
→ Skip Counting by 5s ↗
→ Skip Counting by 10s ↗
Database Tables:
Table: concepts (see BS-CUR-001 in full)
Key fields: concept_id, concept_name, subject, grade_level, board,
estimated_time_minutes, standard_codes[], difficulty_index, status
Table: concept_prerequisites
- id: UUID PK
- concept_id: UUID FK -- the concept requiring the prerequisite
- prerequisite_id: UUID FK -- the prerequisite concept
- relationship: ENUM('required','alternative') DEFAULT 'required'
- alt_group: INTEGER -- for OR-logic grouping
Learning Path Computation:
def get_next_concepts(student_id):
mastered = get_mastered_concepts(student_id)  # all with stars >= 3
all_concepts = get_curriculum_concepts(student.board, student.grade)
unlocked = []
for concept in all_concepts:
if concept.id in mastered:
continue  # already done
prereqs = get_prerequisites(concept.id)
required = [p for p in prereqs if p.relationship == 'required']
alternatives = group_by(prereqs, 'alt_group')
all_required_met = all(p.prerequisite_id in mastered for p in required)
all_alt_groups_met = all(
any(p.prerequisite_id in mastered for p in group)
for group in alternatives.values()
)
if all_required_met and all_alt_groups_met:
unlocked.append(concept)
return sort_by_curriculum_sequence(unlocked)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: DAG validation: System rejects any content upload that creates a cycle (verified on every content change)
• AC2: Learning path computation < 200ms for 200 concepts
• AC3: All Phase 1 concepts have correct prerequisite relationships (verified by curriculum expert review)
• AC4: Admin UI shows visual graph with draggable nodes for content team
• AC5: Every concept maps to at least one CBSE standard code
BS-CUR-002-F | Content Authoring and Approval Workflow
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Curriculum content follows Draft → Review → Published workflow with mandatory human review.
Phase 1 Workflow (simplified):
Content Per Concept (required for Published state):
• Concept name and description
• Learning objectives (1–3 bullet points)
• CBSE standard code(s)
• Grade level and subject
• Prerequisite concept links
• Estimated time to master (minutes)
• RAG source chunks (curriculum text the AI teacher will reference)
• Question bank: ≥ 10 Easy, ≥ 10 Medium, ≥ 5 Hard, ≥ 3 Expert = minimum 28 questions
• Illustration/diagram assets (optional but recommended)
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Content cannot reach Published state without minimum 28 questions
• AC2: Every state transition is logged (who, when, comments)
• AC3: Published content is immutable — edits create a new version
• AC4: Admin can bulk-import concepts from CSV (for initial content loading)
BS-CUR-003-F | RAG Pipeline for Curriculum Alignment
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: CBSE curriculum documents are ingested, chunked, embedded, and stored in a vector database. The AI Teacher retrieves relevant chunks when generating lessons to ensure curriculum alignment.
Pipeline:
Ingest: CBSE syllabus PDFs, NCERT textbook chapters (Grades 1–5 Math + English/Hindi) are loaded
Chunk: Documents are split by learning objective / topic section. Chunk size: ~500 tokens with 100-token overlap
Embed: Each chunk is embedded using sentence-transformers (all-MiniLM-L6-v2 or multilingual-e5-large)
Store: Embeddings + metadata (grade, subject, chapter, board, concept_code) stored in Qdrant
Retrieve (at query time): When AI generates a lesson for concept X:
◦ Construct query: concept name + description + learning objectives
◦ Hybrid search: BM25 keyword match + semantic similarity
◦ Filter: grade <= student's grade, subject = concept's subject, board = student's board
◦ Return top 5 chunks as context for LLM prompt
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
Citation: LLM prompt instructs: "Base your lesson on the following curriculum reference material. Do not make up facts not in the reference."
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: RAG retrieval adds < 300ms to lesson generation
• AC2: Top 5 retrieved chunks are relevant to the concept (validated on 50-concept test set: relevance > 80%)
• AC3: Vector DB handles Phase 1 content (~5,000 chunks) with < 100ms search latency
• AC4: Curriculum updates (new chunks) are indexed within 1 hour of upload
• AC5: All NCERT Grades 1–5 Math and English content is ingested and indexed before Alpha launch

BS-STU-002-F | Student Dashboard — Daily Streak
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P1
Description: A daily streak counter tracks consecutive days the student has completed at least one learning session.
Logic:
• A "learning day" is defined as: Student completed at least 1 concept lesson OR answered at least 10 practice questions
• Streak increments at midnight (device timezone) if learning_day criteria met
• If criteria NOT met for a calendar day, streak resets to 0 (Phase 1 — streak freezes added in Phase 2)
• Streak milestone celebrations: 3, 7, 14, 30, 60, 100 days — special animations

• Total stars
• Alerts: Concepts with < 3 stars after 2+ attempts
API:
GET /api/v1/parent/dashboard
Response 200: {
"children": [{
"student_id": "uuid",
"display_name": "Aarav",
"grade": "class_1",
"board": "cbse",
"streak_days": 5,
"total_stars": 47,

"week_stars": 8,
"week_concepts": 3,
"alerts": [{ "type": "struggling", "concept_name": "Subtraction basics", "stars": 2, "attempts": 3 }]
}]
}

BS-PAY-002-F | Razorpay Payment Integration
Enhanced Requirements (v2.1):• This requirement SHALL define explicit failure handling and graceful degradation paths.• A single authoritative source of truth SHALL be designated for all critical state.• All AI-mediated decisions SHALL be explainable and auditable.• Anti-gaming and abuse-resistance controls SHALL be enforced.• Observability (metrics, logs, alerts) SHALL cover success, failure, and degradation paths.• Cognitive load limits SHALL be enforced as per age group.
Priority: P0
Description: Razorpay is the primary payment gateway, supporting UPI, cards, net banking, and wallets.
Integration Flow:
Parent selects plan → taps "Subscribe"
System creates a Razorpay Subscription object:
`
POST https://api.razorpay.com/v1/subscriptions
{ "plan_id": "plan_xxx", "total_count": 12, "customer_notify": 1 }
`
System opens Razorpay Checkout in a WebView/SDK overlay
Parent selects payment method: UPI / Credit Card / Debit Card / Net Banking / Wallet
Payment completes → Razorpay webhook sends subscription.charged event
System activates subscription, updates parent's billing record
UPI Autopay (Recurring):
• On first payment, Razorpay creates a UPI mandate (e-mandate per RBI guidelines)
• Subsequent months: Auto-charged on billing date
• If payment fails: Razorpay smart retry (3 attempts over 3 days)
• If all retries fail: Downgrade to Free + notify parent
Webhook Handling:
POST /api/v1/webhooks/razorpay (whitelisted Razorpay IPs only)
Events handled:
- subscription.charged → Activate/renew subscription
- subscription.pending → Send reminder notification to parent
- subscription.halted → Downgrade to Free, send notification
- payment.failed → Log failure, trigger retry notification
- refund.processed → Update billing record
Database Table: subscriptions
Database Table: payment_transactions
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: UPI payment completes in under 30 seconds
• AC2: Card payment completes in under 60 seconds
• AC3: Webhook processing completes within 5 seconds of receipt
• AC4: Subscription status is updated within 10 seconds of successful payment
• AC5: Failed payment triggers parent notification within 5 minutes
• AC6: No raw card data is stored — Razorpay tokenisation used exclusively
• AC7: All payment amounts include 18% GST

4. PHASE 2 DETAILED FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENTS (Months 4–6)
Phase 2: Core Learning — Public Beta, 10,000 students, CBSE + ICSE Grades 1–10, Hindi + English + Tamil + Telugu
What a student can do at end of Phase 2 (in addition to all Phase 1 capabilities):
After every concept, student MUST explain it in their own words (voice or text) before final star rating
AI evaluates comprehension across 5 dimensions — star rating now uses weighted formula (self-explanation 40%, practice 30%, application 20%, retention 10%)
Student learns languages via Michel Thomas Method — audio-first building blocks, pronunciation feedback, conversational practice
Student earns badges, coins, and progresses through a Story Mode adventure narrative
Spaced repetition engine schedules daily reviews of mastered concepts — stars can drop and trigger reteaching
Student in Grades 6–10 has access to Science and Social Studies
Mentor can review student progress, spot-check explanations, schedule video calls, and communicate with parents
Parent sees comprehension quality trends, AI-generated insights, and weekly narrative reports
Premium subscribers get mentor access, advanced analytics, and family plan for up to 5 children
Scholarship applicants can apply through the in-app portal
4.1 MODULE: COMPREHENSION CAPTURE ENGINE (CMP)
BS-CMP-001-F | Mandatory Self-Explanation Prompt
Priority: P0
Description: After practice questions and BEFORE the final star rating is assigned, every student MUST explain the concept in their own words. There is no skip option. This is the pedagogical cornerstone of BabySteps.
Trigger: Student completes practice questions for a concept.
Flow by Age Group:
Ages 3–8 (Voice-Only):
AI character says: "You did great with the questions! Now tell me — what did you learn about [Concept Name]? Explain it like you're telling your best friend."
Animated microphone icon pulses — child taps to record
Visual recording indicator: Waveform animation + timer (minimum 10 seconds, maximum 120 seconds)
On stop: System displays "Let me listen to what you said..." (processing indicator)
Whisper STT transcribes audio to text
Transcription displayed back to child with audio playback: "You said: [transcription]. Is that right?"
Child taps ✓ (accept) or 🔄 (re-record — max 3 re-records)
On accept: Transcription + audio sent to AI Comprehension Evaluator
Ages 8–14 (Voice or Text, Voice Encouraged):
Screen shows: "Explain [Concept Name] in your own words. Imagine you're teaching it to a younger student."
Two input options: 🎤 Speak or ⌨️ Type
Voice: Same flow as ages 3–8
Text: Text area with minimum 50 characters, maximum 1,000 characters. Character counter shown. Placeholder text: "Start typing your explanation..."
Submit button disabled until minimum character count met
On submit: Sent to AI Comprehension Evaluator
Ages 14–18 (Text Primary, Voice Optional):
Screen shows: "Explain [Concept Name] in your own words. Include at least one example."
Text area: minimum 100 characters, maximum 2,000 characters
Optional voice toggle available
Submit → AI Comprehension Evaluator
Anti-Gaming Protections:
• Minimum 10 seconds audio recording (shorter recordings rejected: "Tell me a little more!")
• Minimum character counts enforced
• Blank or near-blank submissions rejected with friendly prompt
• Gibberish detection: If STT confidence < 0.3, ask to re-record: "I couldn't quite hear you. Can you try again?"
API Specification:
POST /api/v1/comprehension/submit
Headers: Authorization: Bearer <student_token>
Request: {
"student_id": "uuid",
"concept_id": "uuid",
"session_id": "uuid",
"input_type": "voice",  // "voice" | "text"
"explanation_text": "Addition means putting two numbers together...",
"audio_url": "s3://babysteps-audio/explanations/uuid.opus",  // if voice
"audio_duration_seconds": 35,
"language": "hi",
"attempt_number": 1
}
Response 200: {
"comprehension_id": "uuid",
"status": "evaluating",
"estimated_wait_seconds": 3
}
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Self-explanation prompt appears EVERY time, for EVERY concept — no bypass path exists
• AC2: Voice transcription displayed for confirmation within 3 seconds of recording stop
• AC3: Minimum recording/character limits are enforced (server-side validation)
• AC4: Student can re-record up to 3 times before submitting
• AC5: Works on 2G/3G: Audio compressed to Opus before upload (< 100KB for 30 seconds)
• AC6: Parent can review all child's explanations (audio + text) from parent dashboard
BS-CMP-002-F | AI Comprehension Evaluation Engine
Priority: P0
Description: An AI-powered evaluator scores the student's self-explanation across 5 weighted dimensions, detects parroting, identifies knowledge gaps, and generates targeted follow-up questions.
Evaluation Dimensions:
Anti-Parroting Detection:
Embed student's explanation using multilingual-e5-large
Embed the original lesson text delivered to this student
Compute cosine similarity
If similarity > 0.85: Own Words dimension score = 0, flag as "parroted"
Additional check: Extract key noun phrases from student explanation and lesson; if > 70% overlap with identical phrasing → flag
LLM Evaluation Prompt:
System: You are an expert educational assessor for Indian children.
Evaluate the student's explanation of a concept.
Student profile:
- Age: [age], Grade: [grade], IQ Level: [level]
- Language of explanation: [language]
Concept being explained: [concept_name]
Concept definition (from curriculum): [rag_content]
Learning objectives: [objectives_list]
Lesson text that was delivered to this student: [lesson_text]
Student's explanation: "[explanation_text]"
Evaluate on these 5 dimensions (each 0-100):
1. Accuracy: Are the core facts correct?
2. Completeness: Are all learning objectives addressed?
3. Own Words: Is this genuinely their own understanding? Compare to lesson text.
4. Logical Structure: Is the explanation coherent and organised?
5. Example Quality: Are examples relevant and original?
Also identify:
- Specific knowledge gaps (list)
- Specific misconceptions (list)
- If explanation is incomplete, generate ONE targeted follow-up question
Output ONLY valid JSON:
{
"accuracy_score": 75,
"completeness_score": 60,
"own_words_score": 90,
"structure_score": 70,
"example_quality_score": 50,
"total_score": 71,
"identified_gaps": ["Did not mention carrying in addition"],
"identified_misconceptions": [],
"needs_follow_up": true,
"follow_up_question": "What happens when two digits add up to more than 9?",
"assessment_summary": "Good basic understanding but missed the carry-over concept."
}
Follow-Up Flow:
If total_score >= 70 (High): Proceed to final star calculation. Display: "Great explanation! You really understand [concept]!"
If total_score 40–69 (Medium): Display follow-up question. Student provides additional explanation (1 more attempt). Re-evaluate combined explanation.
If total_score < 40 (Low): Display guiding question. Student provides additional explanation. If still < 40 after 2nd attempt: Record best score, proceed to star calculation, AI notes "Needs reteaching on comprehension."
Maximum 3 explanation attempts total per concept per session.
API Specification:
GET /api/v1/comprehension/:comprehension_id/result
Response 200: {
"comprehension_id": "uuid",
"status": "evaluated",
"total_score": 71,
"dimension_scores": {
"accuracy": 75,
"completeness": 60,
"own_words": 90,
"logical_structure": 70,
"example_quality": 50
},
"parroting_similarity": 0.32,
"is_parroted": false,
"identified_gaps": ["Did not mention carrying in addition"],
"identified_misconceptions": [],
"needs_follow_up": true,
"follow_up_question": "What happens when two digits add up to more than 9?",
"attempt_number": 1,
"max_attempts": 3
}
Database Table: comprehension_records
Data Retention:
• Explanation text + scores: Retained for enrollment + 1 year
• Audio files: Auto-deleted after 30 days UNLESS parent opts in to retain
• Aggregated analytics (no PII): Retained indefinitely
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Evaluation completes within 3 seconds of submission
• AC2: Anti-parroting detection catches > 90% of copy-paste explanations (tested on 200 synthetic cases)
• AC3: Inter-rater reliability: AI scores correlate with human expert scores at κ > 0.7 (validated on 100 explanation sample)
• AC4: Follow-up questions are specific and targeted (not generic "tell me more")
• AC5: Handles code-switching (student mixes Hindi and English) without penalising
• AC6: All scores are deterministic for same input (temperature = 0 for evaluation)
BS-CMP-003-F | Weighted Star Rating (Phase 2 Formula)
Priority: P0
Description: Upgrade the Phase 1 simple percentage-based star rating to the full weighted formula incorporating self-explanation scores.
Phase 2 Star Calculation:
weighted_total = (practice_score × 0.30) + (comprehension_score × 0.40) + (application_score × 0.20) + (retention_score × 0.10)
Where:
- practice_score = percentage correct on practice questions (0-100)
- comprehension_score = best total_score from self-explanation evaluation (0-100)
- application_score = score on application-level questions (novel problems) (0-100)
→ Phase 2: Uses top 3 Hard/Expert practice question scores as proxy
- retention_score = average star rating on this concept from spaced repetition reviews (0-100)
→ First assessment: defaults to practice_score (no reviews yet)
Stars:
0–20 → 1 star
21–40 → 2 stars
41–60 → 3 stars (MINIMUM PASS)
61–80 → 4 stars
81–100 → 5 stars
Migration from Phase 1:
• All existing concept_mastery records retain their Phase 1 star ratings
• On next review (spaced repetition), the Phase 2 formula kicks in
• No retroactive recalculation — stars can only improve or degrade through new assessments
Database Changes (concept_mastery table — additions):
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Star rating reflects all 4 components — verified by test case where high practice but low comprehension yields lower stars than Phase 1
• AC2: Phase 1 students' existing stars are preserved until next assessment
• AC3: Weighted calculation executes < 500ms
• AC4: Star display animation remains the same (visual consistency)
4.2 MODULE: MICHEL THOMAS LANGUAGE ENGINE (LNG)
BS-LNG-001-F | Language Course Structure and Building Blocks
Priority: P0
Description: Each language pair has a structured course of building blocks that teaches conversational fluency using Michel Thomas principles: zero memorisation, building blocks, audio-first, teacher responsibility.
Phase 2 Language Pairs:
Building Block Structure:
Each building block is a self-contained micro-lesson (3–5 minutes):
Introduction (30s): AI says in L1: "Let me teach you something new. Listen carefully. Don't try to remember — just understand."
Presentation (60s): AI speaks the new block in target language. Repeats 2x with L1 bridge. Example: "In Hindi, when you want to say 'I need', you say 'Mujhe chahiye'. Mujhe chahiye. Listen again: Mujhe chahiye."
Comprehension Check (30s): "What does 'Mujhe chahiye' mean?" → Student answers in L1 (voice or tap correct option)
Production Prompt (60s): "Now you try. How would you say 'I need'?" → Student speaks → AI evaluates pronunciation
Combination (60s): "Now let's build. You know 'paani' means water. How would you say 'I need water'?" → Student combines blocks
Interleaving (60s): AI mixes in 1–2 previously learned blocks: "And how would you say 'I need food'?" (using earlier block 'khaana')
Database Table: language_building_blocks
Database Table: language_courses
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Each building block micro-lesson completes in 3–5 minutes
• AC2: Zero text on screen for Stage 1 (Listening) and Stage 2 (Speaking Blocks) — everything is audio
• AC3: AI NEVER says "remember this" or "memorise" — validated by prompt review
• AC4: Previously learned blocks are naturally woven into new block lessons (interleaving)
• AC5: All 8 language pairs have at least 20 published blocks at Phase 2 launch
BS-LNG-002-F | Pronunciation Feedback Engine
Priority: P0
Description: When student speaks in the target language, AI provides real-time pronunciation feedback by comparing phoneme sequences against reference audio.
Technical Flow:
Student speaks the target phrase
Audio → Whisper Large (cloud) → phoneme-level transcription with timestamps
Reference phonemes for the phrase are retrieved from building block record
Phoneme comparison:
◦ Match each student phoneme against reference phoneme sequence
◦ Compute phoneme-level accuracy score (0–100%)
◦ Identify specific mispronounced phonemes
Feedback to student:
◦ Score ≥ 80%: "Bahut achha! That sounded great!" (encouraging, move on)
◦ Score 50–79%: "Good try! Listen to this part again: [AI replays specific segment]. Now try again." (targeted replay)
◦ Score < 50%: "Let me say it slowly for you: [AI speaks phrase at 0.7x speed, word by word]. Your turn!"
Maximum 3 pronunciation attempts per phrase before moving on
Pronunciation Scoring:
phoneme_accuracy = matched_phonemes / total_reference_phonemes × 100
stress_accuracy = correct_stress_positions / total_stress_positions × 100
overall_pronunciation = (phoneme_accuracy × 0.7) + (stress_accuracy × 0.3)
Database Table: pronunciation_attempts
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Pronunciation feedback returned within 2 seconds
• AC2: Phoneme analysis handles Indian-accented speech (trained on Indian speaker corpus)
• AC3: Feedback is specific (not generic "try again") — identifies the exact syllable or sound to improve
• AC4: Ages 3–8: Only positive and encouraging feedback — no "wrong" language
• AC5: Works for Hindi, English, Tamil, Telugu phoneme sets
BS-LNG-003-F | Language Fluency Assessment (5-Star Scale)
Priority: P1
Description: Periodic fluency assessments measure conversational ability on a 5-star scale, separate from academic concept stars.
Assessment Structure (every 10 blocks):
Comprehension Test (2 min): AI speaks 5 sentences in target language. Student identifies meaning (MCQ in L1). Tests listening comprehension.
Production Test (3 min): AI prompts 5 situations in L1, student responds in target language. E.g., "Ask for a glass of water" → Student speaks in Hindi.
Conversation Simulation (3 min): AI conducts a short roleplay conversation (ordering at a shop, introducing family). Evaluated for: vocabulary range, grammatical structure, fluency (hesitation count), pronunciation.
Scoring → Star Rating:
Database Table: language_fluency_assessments
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Assessment takes 8–10 minutes total
• AC2: Conversation simulation feels natural (AI responds contextually, not scripted)
Technology Stack Mandate:All backend services SHALL be implemented in Python. All frontend user interfaces SHALL be implemented in React. Node.js SHALL be used for build tooling, orchestration, and supporting services only. No alternative primary languages or frameworks are permitted unless explicitly approved.
• AC3: Star rating is based on communicative ability, NOT grammar accuracy (per Michel Thomas philosophy)
• AC4: Assessment results visible in both student and parent dashboards
• AC5: Fluency stars are distinct from academic concept stars (separate star count)
4.3 MODULE: SPACED REPETITION ENGINE (SPC)
BS-SPC-001-F | Intensive Phase Pacing Engine
Priority: P0
Description: During the 4-month intensive phase, the system calculates a personalised daily learning pace to complete the year's curriculum in 16 weeks.
Pacing Calculation:
total_concepts = count_concepts(student.board, student.grade, student.subjects)
available_days = 112 - holidays(student.state) - buffer_days(7)
daily_target = ceil(total_concepts / available_days)
Adjusted by IQ Level:
Level 3: daily_target × 1.3 (3-4 concepts/day typical)
Level 2: daily_target × 1.0 (2-3 concepts/day typical)
Level 1: daily_target × 0.7 (1-2 concepts/day typical)
Weekly Milestone Checks (Every Friday):
Calculate: expected_concepts_completed = daily_target × days_elapsed
Compare to actual_concepts_completed
If behind by > 20%:
◦ Push notification to parent: "[Child] is a bit behind schedule. Encouraging 15 extra minutes of learning this week could help!"
◦ AI adjusts: Slightly increase pace for next week, prioritise high-weight concepts
If ahead by > 20%:
◦ Celebrate: "Amazing progress! [Child] is ahead of schedule!"
◦ AI offers: Enrichment activities, deeper dives, or preview of next grade topics
If exactly on track: "Perfect pace! Keep going!"
API Specification:
GET /api/v1/pacing/:student_id
Response 200: {
"phase": "intensive",
"total_concepts": 180,
"completed_concepts": 45,
"daily_target": 2,
"days_elapsed": 25,
"days_remaining": 87,
"pace_status": "on_track",  // "ahead" | "on_track" | "behind" | "critical"
"expected_by_today": 50,
"weekly_velocity": 14,
"projected_completion_date": "2026-08-15",
"next_milestone": { "date": "2026-06-20", "target_concepts": 60 }
}
Database Table: pacing_records
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Pacing calculation generated within 5 seconds of enrollment
• AC2: Daily target adjusts automatically after each milestone check
• AC3: Parent notification for "behind" status sent within 1 hour of Friday milestone check
• AC4: Early completers (finish before 16 weeks) automatically transition to spaced repetition phase
• AC5: Handles mid-year enrollments (calculates from enrollment date, not academic year start)
BS-SPC-002-F | Spaced Repetition Review Scheduler
Priority: P0
Description: After a concept reaches 3+ stars and the student enters the spaced repetition phase, the system schedules periodic reviews at increasing intervals using a modified Leitner algorithm.
Algorithm — Modified Leitner with Star-Based Intervals:
On concept reaching 3+ stars:
next_review = calculate_interval(star_rating)
Interval Table:
5★: Review at +14 days, +30 days, +60 days, +120 days
4★: Review at +7 days, +14 days, +30 days, +60 days
3★: Review at +3 days, +7 days, +14 days, +30 days, +60 days
On each review:
Student answers 2-3 questions + brief self-explanation (30-second minimum)
Star rating recalculated using Phase 2 weighted formula
If new_stars >= previous_stars:
Move to next interval level (longer gap)
If new_stars < 3:
IMMEDIATELY re-enter intensive mode for this concept
Reteaching triggered (BS-AIE-003-F)
If 5★ maintained for 3 consecutive reviews:
Move to 4-month maintenance cycle
Daily Review Queue Generation:
• Runs at midnight (student's timezone) or on app open
• Selects 5–10 concepts where next_review_date <= today
• Composition: 70% scheduled reviews + 30% interleaved (random concepts from other subjects to promote cross-topic connections)
• Prioritised: Overdue reviews first, then by star rating (lower stars = higher priority)
• Estimated time: 15–25 minutes for daily review
Review Session UI:
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ 📖 Daily Review (7 concepts today)          │
│ ⏱️ ~20 minutes                              │
│                                             │
│ 1. ⭐⭐⭐⭐ Addition (2-digit)    [Review →]  │
│ 2. ⭐⭐⭐  Subtraction basics     [Review →]  │
│ 3. ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Hindi vowels          [Review →]  │
│ 4. 🔀   Science: Plants (interleaved)      │
│ 5. ⭐⭐⭐  Multiplication (2-digit)[Review →] │
│ ...                                         │
│                                             │
│ Progress: 0/7 complete                      │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────┘
API Specification:
GET /api/v1/reviews/:student_id/today
Response 200: {
"review_date": "2026-07-15",
"reviews": [
{
"concept_id": "uuid",
"concept_name": "Addition (2-digit)",
"current_stars": 4,
"last_reviewed": "2026-07-01",
"review_type": "scheduled",  // "scheduled" | "interleaved"
"question_count": 3,
"requires_explanation": true,
"estimated_minutes": 3
}
],
"total_estimated_minutes": 20
}
POST /api/v1/reviews/:student_id/complete
Request: {
"concept_id": "uuid",
"question_responses": [...],
"comprehension_id": "uuid"
}
Response 200: {
"previous_stars": 4,
"new_stars": 4,
"next_review_date": "2026-08-14",
"interval_days": 30,
"status": "maintained"  // "improved" | "maintained" | "declined" | "reteach_required"
}
Database Changes (concept_mastery table — additions):
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Daily review queue generated within 5 seconds
• AC2: Star drop below 3 triggers reteaching within the same session (no delay)
• AC3: Review intervals are correctly calculated per the interval table
• AC4: 5★ × 3 consecutive reviews → 4-month maintenance confirmed by test
• AC5: Interleaved reviews (30%) are from different subjects than scheduled reviews
• AC6: Overdue reviews are prioritised (oldest first)
BS-SPC-003-F | Academic Calendar and Phase Transition
Priority: P1
Description: Admin configures the academic calendar. System auto-transitions students between intensive and spaced repetition phases.
Configuration:
academic_calendar:
year_start: 2026-06-01
intensive_phase_weeks: 16
intensive_phase_end: 2026-09-21  // auto-calculated
holidays:
- { date: 2026-08-15, name: "Independence Day", national: true }
- { date: 2026-10-02, name: "Gandhi Jayanti", national: true }
- { date: 2026-10-12, name: "Dussehra", national: true }
- { date: 2026-11-01, name: "Diwali", national: true }
// ... all national holidays pre-populated
state_holidays:
- { state: "maharashtra", date: 2026-05-01, name: "Maharashtra Day" }
// ...
Phase Transition Logic:
• On intensive_phase_end date OR when student completes all concepts (whichever is first):
◦ Student status → 'spaced_repetition'
◦ All concepts with stars >= 3 enter review schedule
◦ Concepts with stars < 3 remain in intensive mode (continued alongside reviews)
◦ Parent notified: "Great news! [Child] has entered the reinforcement phase."
• Late completers: If not all concepts done by end date, system auto-transitions and remaining concepts are flagged as priority
Acceptance Criteria:
• AC1: Phase transition happens automatically on the configured date (midnight batch job)
• AC2: Early completers transition immediately upon completing last concept
• AC3: Holidays are pre-populated for all Indian national holidays
• AC4: Parent sees current phase and estimated transition date in dashboard
